## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (ordinary differential rate laws)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is the time-derivative of a concentration A, which is the standard object modeled by chemical kinetics rate laws. With only (t, A) available, the most common mechanistic structures are mass-action power laws in A, linear relaxation to equilibrium, and time-dependent effective rate coefficients (e.g., due to changing conditions or catalyst deactivation).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order consumption/production: dA_dt = c0 (constant-rate regime; excess reactant/catalyst-limited)
- First-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decay, radioactive-like, pseudo-first-order kinetics)
- First-order with source term: dA_dt = c0 - c1 * A (approach to steady state in well-mixed reactor with feed/decay)
- Second-order decay (single-species effective): dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular/self-reaction or lumped second-order behavior)
- General n-th order rate law: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (mass-action-like power-law kinetics over a range)
- Reversible relaxation to equilibrium (linearized): dA_dt = c0 * (c1 - A) (approach to equilibrium concentration c1)
- Autocatalytic/logistic-like kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (self-accelerating reaction with limiting capacity/precursor depletion)
- Product inhibition / self-limitation (rational): dA_dt = -c0 * A / (c1 + A) (rate reduces at high A due to inhibition/complexation)
- Time-dependent first-order (activation/deactivation): dA_dt = -c0 * exp(-c1 * t) * A (effective rate decreases over time; catalyst deactivation/aging)
- Time-dependent n-th order: dA_dt = -c0 * (t + c1)**c2 * A**c3 (ramping conditions or changing environment captured phenomenologically)
- Stretched-exponential-type kinetics (in derivative form): dA_dt = -c0 * t**c1 * A (distributed-rate / dispersive kinetics; often arises in heterogeneous media)
- Empirical mixed-order: dA_dt = -c0 * A - c1 * A**2 (parallel pathways: unimolecular + bimolecular)
- Finite-time quench / delayed start (smooth step): dA_dt = -c0 * A * (1 / (1 + exp(c1 * (c2 - t)))) (reaction switches on/off around time c2 due to mixing/illumination)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope ŌåÆ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects ŌåÆ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay ŌåÆ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior ŌåÆ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects ŌåÆ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Stoichiometric consumption typically implies dA_dt is negative and monotone in A; positive dA_dt suggests net generation/feed or reversal toward equilibrium.
- Mass-action mechanisms often appear as integer/near-integer powers of A in dA_dt (A, A**2, A**3); non-integer powers can indicate effective/heterogeneous or lumped kinetics.
- Linear form c0 - c1*A indicates a stable steady state A_ss = c0/c1 (common for CSTR-like balance or relaxation to equilibrium).
- Presence of (c1 - A) or A*(c1 - A) suggests an identifiable limiting concentration (equilibrium or capacity), giving sigmoidal/peaked rate vs A.
- Rational inhibition forms A/(c1 + A) imply diminishing marginal rate at high A (complexation, inhibition, saturation of reactive sites).
- Explicit time factors exp(-c*t) multiplying A indicate time-varying reactivity (catalyst deactivation, fouling, reagent depletion not explicitly modeled).
- Polynomial-in-time prefactors (t + c)**p suggest externally ramped conditions (e.g., programmed heating/illumination) when temperature/intensity variables are omitted.
- Mixed linear + quadratic terms (-c0*A - c1*A**2) indicate parallel reaction channels whose dominance changes with concentration.
- A-only ODEs with stable fixed points can be checked by setting dA_dt = 0; the number of real roots hints at single-step vs multi-regime behavior.
